       <div class="h5">
        <a href="/staff/gerhardus-kemp/">
         Professor Gerhard Kemp
        </a>
       </div>
       <div class="h5 subheading">
        Professor in International and Transnational Criminal Justice
       </div>
      </div>
      <p class="search-result-teaser">
       Gerhard Kemp is a professor of law and specialises in international and transnational criminal justice, comparative criminal law, international humanitarian law and transitional justice. He is an Alexander von Humboldt Research Fellow and a former Senior Research Fellow of the Robert Bosch Stiftung in Berlin, Germany.
      </p>

Getting the Professor Links and Names¶

In [6]:
urls_derby = [] 
prof_names_derby = []
for data in soup_1.find_all('div', class_='h5'):
    for a in data.find_all('a'):
        urls_derby.append(a.get('href')) #for getting link
        prof_names_derby.append(a.text) #for getting text between the link
        


prof_link_derby= []
for lk in urls_derby:
    url = 'https://www.derby.ac.uk/'+lk
    prof_link_derby.append(url)
    
prof_link_derby

Research Areas of Professors¶

In [8]:
sum_derby = []
for data in soup_1.find_all('p', class_='search-result-teaser'):
    sum_derby.append(data.text)
    
sum_derby
Out[8]:
['Gerhard Kemp is a professor of law and specialises in international and transnational criminal justice, comparative criminal law, international humanitarian law and transitional justice. He is an Alexander von Humboldt Research Fellow and a former Senior Research Fellow of the Robert Bosch Stiftung in Berlin, Germany.',
 'Zafar is a senior lecturer in law on the LLM  Legal Practice Course. Zafar has over 27 years experience working as a Partner in large regional and national solicitors firms. He brings a wealth of experience to the Derby Law School.',
 "Steve Bravery is a Senior Lecturer in\xa0the University of Derby's Law School, primarily teaching modules on the LLM LPC course. His specialisms relate to the criminal justice system including criminal litigation and the parole process.",
 'As a Senior Lecturer in Law, Lisa Cherkassky teaches criminal law and medical law to law undergraduates, and has published widely in both fields, on topics such as causation, HIV transmission, genocide, saviour siblings, liver transplants, abortion law, and the welfare of the child.',
 'Karen is a\xa0practising solicitor with Flint Bishop and is also a associate lecturer in licensing law.\xa0',
 'As a Lecturer in Law, Liz teaches the fundamental principles of the English legal system and Family Law. She is also First Year Tutor on the LLB course.\xa0',
 'Jo Drummond Child is a senior lecturer in law and the programme leader for the BA (Hons) Law with\xa0Foundation Year. Prior to joining the\xa0University,\xa0Jo was a barrister. Jo is also the academic lead for collaborative programmes for law and social science partnerships.',
 'Christie is a senior lecturer in the Derby Law School with responsibility for leading modules on European Union law, European Union Trade Law and Land Law.',
 'Dr Eghosa Ekhator is a Senior Lecturer in Law. He joined the University of Derby in September 2019 from the University of Chester, where he taught on both undergraduate and postgraduate levels. His primary areas of research are International Environmental Law (especially Environmental Justice issues in developing countries and the African Union) and Natural Resources Governance.',
 'George is a Senior Lecturer in Law and specialise in teaching public law, human rights, and crime.']

    <!-- Design Body Start -->
    <!-- Paint Layout - LSBU - Default Start -->
    <div class="row">
     <!-- Asset Contents Start -->
     <div class="col-12 col-tab-9 left-col">
      <div id="department">
       <div class="clear">
       </div>
       <div class="course-staff-listing">
        <div class="row">
         <div class="col-12 col-sm-4">
          <a href="https://www.lsbu.ac.uk/about-us/people/people-finder/michael-abiodun-olatokun">
           <img alt="Michael Abiodun Olatokun" src="https://www.lsbu.ac.uk/__data/assets/image/0005/277376/Michael-Olatokun-image.jpg"/>
          </a>
         </div>
         <div class="col-12 col-sm-8">
          <h3 class="media-heading">
           <a href="https://www.lsbu.ac.uk/about-us/people/people-finder/michael-abiodun-olatokun">
            <span>
             Dr Michael Abiodun Olatokun
            </span>
           </a>
          </h3>
          <div>
           <span>
            Job title:
           </span>
           Lecturer
          </div>
          <div>
           <span>
            Email:
           </span>
           <a href="mailto:olatokum@lsbu.ac.uk">
            olatokum@lsbu.ac.uk
           </a>
          </div>
          <br/>
          <p>
           Michael Abiodun Olatokun is researcher, activist and educator.Since 2016 he has been a Research Fellow at the Bingham Centre for the Rule of Law where he is also the Head of Public and Youth Engagement. Michaels work at the Bingham Centre involves educating young people across the world about democracy and human rights. He recently created an online course, 'Citizenship and the Rule of Law', which over 5,000 students have participated in thus far.He is the Coordinator of 'The Rule of Law for Citizenship Education', a UK-wide programme for secondary school students. As a result of the success of this work, Michael was asked to join the Solicitor General's Public Legal Education Committee in 2017. He was a co-author of the minister's vision statement in 2018.
          </p>
          <p>
           In the last few years Michael has contributed to several public inquiries relating to areas of his research. The bodies conducting these inquiries have frequently cited his evidence in producing final recommendations for government decision makers, including the House of Commons Justice Select Committee inquiry into reform of courts and tribunals , the Draft Commissioner for Children and Young People (Jersey) Law 201- Scrutiny review - Care of Children in Jersey Review Panel and the final report of the House of Lords Ad Hoc Select Committee on Citizenship and Civic Engagement.
          </p>
          <p>
           Michael began his career as a community organiser encouraging young people and disenfranchised groups to participate in public life. He has led voter registration projects that have successfully registered hundreds of thousands of first-time voters, working with the Cabinet Office and other partners to promote voter engagement in the run-up to the 2016 European Union Referendum. The University of Nottingham gave Michael an 'Alumni Laureate Award' to recognise his democratic engagement work and he was named a (fee-waiving) Fellow of the Royal Society of the Arts in 2017.
          </p>
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
    </div>
   </div>

    <span>
     Dr Ozan Kamiloglu
    </span>
   </a>
  </h3>
  <div>
   <span>
    Job title:
   </span>
   Lecturer
  </div>
  <div>
   <span>
    Email:
   </span>
   <a href="mailto:kamilogo@lsbu.ac.uk">
    kamilogo@lsbu.ac.uk
   </a>
  </div>
  <br/>
  <p>
   Dr. Kamiloglu joined to Department of Law in 2020, and he specialises in effects of social movements on law and understanding of legality. Previously he worked in Universities of Essex, SOAS and Birkbeck College where he had gained his PhD degree in Law.
  </p>
  <p>
   Dr. Kamiloglu is an active researcher focusing on; use and narrations of violence in domestic and international law, how intersections of gender, class and history shapes the law today; ways in which human rights discourses that born out of social movements in the Global South; and roles of responsibility and care in relation to global history of human rights.
  </p>
  <p>
   He is active in various community projects around the world and took part in various initiatives to protect academics from the Global South and academic freedom of speech.
  </p>

 <div class="col-12 col-sm-4">
  <a href="https://www.lsbu.ac.uk/about-us/people/people-finder/cameron-giles">
   <img alt="Cameron Giles" src=""/>
  </a>
 </div>
 <div class="col-12 col-sm-8">
  <h3 class="media-heading">
   <a href="https://www.lsbu.ac.uk/about-us/people/people-finder/cameron-giles">
    <span>
     Emma Rehal-Wilde
    </span>
   </a>
  </h3>
  <div>
   <span>
    Job title:
   </span>
   Lecturer
  </div>
  <div>
   <span>
    Email:
   </span>
   <a href="mailto:gilesc4@lsbu.ac.uk">
    gilesc4@lsbu.ac.uk
   </a>
  </div>
  <br/>
  <p>
   Cameron Giles is a Lecturer in the Law Division. His academic interests focus on Criminal Law, Legal Theory, and LGBTQ issues in Law.
  </p>
  <p>
   Cameron completed the MLaw (Exempting) Degree at Northumbria University and was called to the Bar by the Inner Temple in 2016. He then went on to gain an LLM in Legal and Political Theory from the University of York, before returning to Northumbria to undertake a PhD on HIV transmission offences, which he is currently finalising.
  </p>
  <p>
   Cameron teaches on multiple modules within the Law division, including Criminal Law and Introduction to Contract and Tort, and previously taught as an Associate Lecturer at Northumbria. Cameron is keen on integrating experiential learning and contemporary legal research into his teaching.
  </p>
  <p>
   Cameron has written multiple academic and non-academic pieces based on his research, addressing the role of digital evidence in HIV transmission cases, online LBGTQ identities and the punishment of offenders. In addition to several conference papers, Cameron has presented invited seminars at Northumbria and UCL and recently appeared on
   <em>
    The Diversity in Research Podcast.
   </em>
  </p>
  <p>
   Cameron is currently an Assistant Editor for the International Journal of Gender, Sexuality and Law.
  </p>

sum_lsbu
Out[20]:
["Michael Abiodun Olatokun is researcher, activist and educator.\xa0\xa0Since 2016 he has been a Research Fellow at the Bingham Centre for the Rule of Law where he is also the Head of Public and Youth Engagement. Michaels work at the Bingham Centre involves educating young people across the world about democracy and human rights. He recently created an online course, 'Citizenship and the Rule of Law', which over 5,000 students have participated in thus far.\xa0\xa0He is the Coordinator of 'The Rule of Law for Citizenship Education', a UK-wide programme for secondary school students. As a result of the success of this work, Michael was asked to join the Solicitor General's Public Legal Education Committee in 2017. He was a co-author of the minister's vision statement in 2018.",
 'In the last few years Michael has contributed to several public inquiries relating to areas of his research. The bodies conducting these inquiries have frequently cited his evidence in producing final recommendations for government decision makers, including the House of Commons Justice Select Committee inquiry into reform of courts and tribunals , the Draft Commissioner for Children and Young People (Jersey) Law 201- Scrutiny review - Care of Children in Jersey Review Panel and the final report of the House of Lords Ad Hoc Select Committee on Citizenship and Civic Engagement.',
 "Michael began his career as a community organiser encouraging young people and disenfranchised groups to participate in public life. He has led voter registration projects that have successfully registered hundreds of thousands of first-time voters, working with the Cabinet Office and other partners to promote voter engagement in the run-up to the 2016 European Union Referendum. The University of Nottingham gave Michael an 'Alumni Laureate Award' to recognise his democratic engagement work and he was named a (fee-waiving) Fellow of the Royal Society of the Arts in 2017.",
 'Louise is an Associate Professor specialising in Land Law, as well as Director of Student Recruitment and Admissions for the Schools of Law and Social Sciences and Arts and Creative Industries.',
 'Tracey Aquino is an accomplished and innovative lecturer in law with a comprehensive blend of hands-on professional and academic teaching experience.',
 'Prof. Craig Barker is the Dean of the School of Law and Social Sciences and a Professor of International Law. Appointed in 2015, Prof. Barker has taught extensively in the areas of domestic and international law, as well as international politics. He is a leading international expert on issues relating to diplomatic law.',
 'Vanessa is the Director of Education and Student Experience of the School of Law and Social Sciences.',
 'Alan is a Senior Lecturer in Law and a practising barrister. Alan has Senior Fellow status with the Higher Education Authority.',
 'Lionel Blackman is a solicitor-advocate, the first to win a case in the House of Lords.\xa0\xa0He is Director of the Solicitors International Human Rights Group. He lectures frequently at LSBU and overseas.',
 "Sara is a housing solicitor specialising in landlord and tenant law. She works in London South Bank University's Legal Advice Clinic.",
 "Senior Law Lecturer, Director of Studies for single honours full time LLB (Hons), admissions tutor for the LLB (Hons) and member of London South Bank University's Employability Committee.",
 'Catherine Evans joined the University in 2015, previously having worked as the Legal Director of Southwark Law Centre. She trained at TV Edwards Solicitors and then moved on to Mary Ward Legal Centre in Central London.',
 'Farnush Ghadery is a Lecturer in Law at London South Bank University.',
 'Robert Hush is a Senior Lecturer in Law and a practicing family law solicitor, specialising in family law.',
 'Dr James specialises in English Legal System, the first year student experience, student mobility, and EU law.\xa0\xa0Within the field of EU law her particular interests are EU citizenship, EU Higher Education law, Erasmus student mobility, and the Area of Freedom, Security and Justice.',
 'Dr Kalul is a lecturer in Law in the School of Law and Social Sciences.',
 'Dr. Kamiloglu joined to Department of Law in 2020, and he specialises in effects of social movements on law and understanding of legality. Previously he worked in Universities of Essex, SOAS and Birkbeck College where he had gained his PhD degree in Law.',
 'Dr. Kamiloglu is an active researcher focusing on; use and narrations of violence in domestic and international law, how intersections of gender, class and history shapes the law today; ways in which human rights discourses that born out of social movements in the Global South; and roles of responsibility and care in relation to global history of human rights.',
 'He is active in various community projects around the world and took part in various initiatives to protect academics from the Global South and academic freedom of speech.',
 'Sonal Khamajeet is a passionate law lecturer and researcher with a particular expertise in Law of Equity and Trust, Human Rights and Land Law.',
 'John Koo is subject leader for European Union law. His research interests cover EU asylum law and the impact of Brexit on legal education. He is Course Director for the Law Conversion course (PG Diploma/CPE).',

 'Emma holds a BA Hons in Politics & Sociology from the University of Warwick.  'Cameron Giles is a Lecturer in the Law Division. His academic interests focus on Criminal Law, Legal Theory, and LGBTQ issues in Law.',
 'Cameron completed the MLaw (Exempting) Degree at Northumbria University and was called to the Bar by the Inner Temple in 2016. He then went on to gain an LLM in Legal and Political Theory from the University of York, before returning to Northumbria to undertake a PhD on HIV transmission offences, which he is currently finalising.',
 'Cameron teaches on multiple modules within the Law division, including Criminal Law and Introduction to Contract and Tort, and previously taught as an Associate Lecturer at Northumbria. Cameron is keen on integrating experiential learning and contemporary legal research into his teaching.',
 'Cameron has written multiple academic and non-academic pieces based on his research, addressing the role of digital evidence in HIV transmission cases, online LBGTQ identities and the punishment of offenders. (0, "Michael Abiodun Olatokun is researcher, activist and educator.\xa0\xa0Since 2016 he has been a Research Fellow at the Bingham Centre for the Rule of Law where he is also the Head of Public and Youth Engagement. Michaels work at the Bingham Centre involves educating young people across the world about democracy and human rights. He recently created an online course, 'Citizenship and the Rule of Law', which over 5,000 students have participated in thus far.\xa0\xa0He is the Coordinator of 'The Rule of Law for Citizenship Education', a UK-wide programme for secondary school students. As a result of the success of this work, Michael was asked to join the Solicitor General's Public Legal Education Committee in 2017. He was a co-author of the minister's vision statement in 2018.")
(1, 'Louise is an Associate Professor specialising in Land Law, as well as Director of Student Recruitment and Admissions for the Schools of Law and Social Sciences and Arts and Creative Industries.')
(2, 'Tracey Aquino is an accomplished and innovative lecturer in law with a comprehensive blend of hands-on professional and academic teaching experience.')
(3, 'Prof. Craig Barker is the Dean of the School of Law and Social Sciences and a Professor of International Law. Appointed in 2015, Prof. Barker has taught extensively in the areas of domestic and international law, as well as international politics. He is a leading international expert on issues relating to diplomatic law.')
(4, 'Vanessa is the Director of Education and Student Experience of the School of Law and Social Sciences.')
(5, 'Alan is a Senior Lecturer in Law and a practising barrister. Alan has Senior Fellow status with the Higher Education Authority.')
(6, 'Lionel Blackman is a solicitor-advocate, the first to win a case in the House of Lords.\xa0\xa0He is Director of the Solicitors International Human Rights Group. He lectures frequently at LSBU and overseas.')
(7, "Sara is a housing solicitor specialising in landlord and tenant law. She works in London South Bank University's Legal Advice Clinic.")
(8, "Senior Law Lecturer, Director of Studies for single honours full time LLB (Hons), admissions tutor for the LLB (Hons) and member of London South Bank University's Employability Committee.")

(10, 'Farnush Ghadery is a Lecturer in Law at London South Bank University.')
(11, 'Robert Hush is a Senior Lecturer in Law and a practicing family law solicitor, specialising in family law.')
(12, 'Dr James specialises in English Legal System, the first year student experience, student mobility, and EU law.\xa0\xa0Within the field of EU law her particular interests are EU citizenship, EU Higher Education law, Erasmus student mobility, and the Area of Freedom, Security and Justice.')
(13, 'Dr Kalul is a lecturer in Law in the School of Law and Social Sciences.')
(14, 'Dr. Kamiloglu joined to Department of Law in 2020, and he specialises in effects of social movements on law and understanding of legality. Previously he worked in Universities of Essex, SOAS and Birkbeck College where he had gained his PhD degree in Law.')
(15, 'Dr. Kamiloglu is an active researcher focusing on; use and narrations of violence in domestic and international law, how intersections of gender, class and history shapes the law today; ways in which human rights discourses that born out of social movements in the Global South; and roles of responsibility and care in relation to global history of human rights.')
(16, 'Sonal Khamajeet is a passionate law lecturer and researcher with a particular expertise in Law of Equity and Trust, Human Rights and Land Law.')
(17, 'John Koo is subject leader for European Union law. His research interests cover EU asylum law and the impact of Brexit on legal education. He is Course Director for the Law Conversion course (PG Diploma/CPE).')
(18, 'Michael teaches contract law on the CPE and aspects of international business law on the LLM in International Commercial Law.')
(19, 'Emma is in the Department of Law within the School of Law and Social Sciences. She teaches on both the LLB and LLM courses.')
(20, 'Emma qualified as a solicitor in 2008 and worked in corporate social responsibility and pro bono management within the legal sector for 12 years before moving into academia.\xa0\xa0Her particular interests are in access to justice and development.')
(21, 'Emma holds a BA Hons in Politics & Sociology from the University of Warwick. She completed the Graduate Diploma in Law and Legal Practice Course at the College of Law (now University of Law), and holds a LLM in International Economic Law, Justice and Development from Birkbeck, University of London.')
(22, 'Cameron Giles is a Lecturer in the Law Division. His academic interests focus on Criminal Law, Legal Theory, and LGBTQ issues in Law.')
(23, 'Cameron completed the MLaw (Exempting) Degree at Northumbria University and was called to the Bar by the Inner Temple in 2016. He then went on to gain an LLM in Legal and Political Theory from the University of York, before returning to Northumbria to undertake a PhD on HIV transmission offences, which he is currently finalising.')
(24, 'Cameron teaches on multiple modules within the Law division, including Criminal Law and Introduction to Contract and Tort, and previously taught as an Associate Lecturer at Northumbria. Cameron is keen on integrating experiential learning and contemporary legal research into his teaching.')
(25, 'Cameron has written multiple academic and non-academic pieces based on his research, addressing the role of digital evidence in HIV transmission cases, online LBGTQ identities and the punishment of offenders. In addition to several conference papers, Cameron has presented invited seminars at Northumbria and UCL and recently appeared on The Diversity in Research Podcast.')
(26, 'Cameron is currently an Assistant Editor for the International Journal of Gender, Sexuality and Law.')
(27, 'Dr Michael Rodney is a Senior Lecturer in the School of Law and Social Sciences.')
(28, 'Alan is a Senior Law Lecturer. He is a Senior Fellow of the Higher Education Academy and a practising solicitor. He specialises in clinical legal education, civil justice and social welfare law.')
(29, 'Chris is the Course Director of the LLM International Commercial Law. He specialises in contract law, company law and the international sale of goods and is a Senior Fellow of the Higher Education Academy.')
(30, 'Kim Silver is a Senior Lecturer in the Law Division, where she leads final year project modules.')
(31, 'Katherine Stylianou specialises in the following subjects:\xa0\xa0Alternative Dispute Resolution, Mediation Skills and the Law and Analysis of Evidence (mainly Criminal).')
(32, 'Caron has lectured and tutored at LSBU for over 20 years and has used her experience of legal practice to enhance the practical legal content of the subjects that she teaches.')
(33, 'Andy Unger is Head of the Law Division and a Solicitor. He specialises in Legal Education, International Human Rights and Medical Law & Ethics.')
(34, 'Max is deeply interested in the interaction between the common law (which judges make) and social needs and norms. He explores these through tort law and through philosophical scholarship.')
(35, 'Paul is a Senior Lecturer in the School of Law and Social Sciences.')

'Cameron Giles is a Lecturer in the Law Division. His academic interests focus on Criminal Law, Legal Theory, and LGBTQ issues in Law.Cameron completed the MLaw (Exempting) Degree at Northumbria University and was called to the Bar by the Inner Temple in 2016. He then went on to gain an LLM in Legal and Political Theory from the University of York, before returning to Northumbria to undertake a PhD on HIV transmission offences, which he is currently finalising.Cameron teaches on multiple modules within the Law division, including Criminal Law and Introduction to Contract and Tort, and previously taught as an Associate Lecturer at Northumbria. Cameron is keen on integrating experiential learning and contemporary legal research into his teaching.Cameron has written multiple academic and non-academic pieces based on his research, addressing the role of digital evidence in HIV transmission cases, online LBGTQ identities and the punishment of offenders. In addition to several conference papers, Cameron has presented invited seminars at Northumbria and UCL and recently appeared on The Diversity in Research Podcast.Cameron is currently an Assistant Editor for the International Journal of Gender, Sexuality and Law.'

url3 = 'https://www.dur.ac.uk/law/staff/'
page3 = requests.get(url3)
soup3 = BeautifulSoup(page3.content, 'html.parser')

page3.url
Out[24]:
'https://www.dur.ac.uk/law/staff/'

Durham Law professors and links to their profiles¶

In [25]:
urls_durham = [] 
prof_names_durham = []
for data in soup3.find_all('tbody'):
    
    for a in data.find_all('td'):

        for url in a.find_all('a'):
            #for getting link
            urls_durham.append(url.get("href"))
            
            #for getting text between the link
            prof_names_durham.append(a.text)
In [26]:
mainurls3 = []
profnames3 = []

for ur in urls_durham:
    if '?id=' in ur:
        mainurls3.append(ur)
        
for nm in prof_names_durham:
    if (nm.startswith('Mr') or nm.startswith('Dr') or nm.startswith('Mrs') or nm.startswith('Pr') or nm.startswith('Rt') or nm.startswith('Th') or nm.startswith(' Me') or nm.startswith('Da')  or nm.startswith('Miss') or nm.startswith('Ms')):
        profnames3.append(nm)
    elif 'Jason' in nm:
        profnames3.append(nm)
        
print(len(mainurls3))
print(len(profnames3))

89
89
In [27]:
prof_ns =list(profnames3[11:24])
print(prof_ns)


durhurls = []
for lk in mainurls3:
    if not lk.startswith("https://www.dur.ac.uk/"):
        url = 'https://www.dur.ac.uk/'+lk
        durhurls.append(url)
        
        
dururls = durhurls[11:24]
print('\n\n',dururls)

Removing Punctuation and converting to lower case¶

In [49]:
punctuation = """!"#$%&'()*+,-./:;<=>?@[\]^_`{|}~"""
Final_DF['txt_without_punc'] = Final_DF['Summary & Research areas'].str.lower().apply(lambda x: ''.join(ch for ch in x if ch not in set(punctuation)))
Final_DF['txt_without_punc'][0]
Out[49]:
'gerhard kemp is a professor of law and specialises in international and transnational criminal justice comparative criminal law international humanitarian law and transitional justice he is an alexander von humboldt research fellow and a former senior research fellow of the robert bosch stiftung in berlin germany'

In [56]:
import nltk

w_tokenizer = nltk.tokenize.WhitespaceTokenizer()
lemmatizer = nltk.stem.WordNetLemmatizer()

def lemmatize_text(Stemm_text):
    return [lemmatizer.lemmatize(w) for w in w_tokenizer.tokenize(Stemm_text)]

Final_DF['text_lemmatized'] = (Final_DF['Stemm_text'].apply(lemmatize_text)).str.join(' ')

from collections import defaultdict

class invertedIndex(object):
    def __init__(self,docs):
        self.docSets = defaultdict(set)
        for index, doc in enumerate(docs):
            for term in doc.split():
                self.docSets[term].add(index)
                
        print(self.docSets)
        
    def search(self,term):
        return self.docSets[term]

    
docs=[sent for sent in Final_DF.clean_text]
i=invertedIndex(docs)

Research areas of Professor is : Cameron Giles is a Lecturer in the Law Division. His academic interests focus on Criminal Law, Legal Theory, and LGBTQ issues in Law.Cameron completed the MLaw (Exempting) Degree at Northumbria University and was called to the Bar by the Inner Temple in 2016. He then went on to gain an LLM in Legal and Political Theory from the University of York, before returning to Northumbria to undertake a PhD on HIV transmission offences, which he is currently finalising.Cameron teaches on multiple modules within the Law division, including Criminal Law and Introduction to Contract and Tort, and previously taught as an Associate Lecturer at Northumbria. Cameron is keen on integrating experiential learning and contemporary legal research into his teaching.Cameron has written multiple academic and non-academic pieces based on his research, addressing the role of digital evidence in HIV transmission cases, online LBGTQ identities and the punishment of offenders. In addition to several conference papers, Cameron has presented invited seminars at Northumbria and UCL and recently appeared on The Diversity in Research Podcast.Cameron is currently an Assistant Editor for the International Journal of Gender, Sexuality and Law.
